<div id="review_99490596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99490596" />
    <a title="Nancy Meservier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3363188-nancy-meservier"><img alt="Nancy Meservier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561570725p2/3363188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99490596?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Meservier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Meservier" href="/user/show/3363188-nancy-meservier">Nancy Meservier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3363188-nancy-meservier?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3363188-nancy-meservier?shelf=short-fiction">short-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99490596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7666095386869004079">Tales of the Otherworld is the second collection of short fiction which takes place in the Otherworld universe. The first collection, Men of the Otherworld, was unique as it almost read like a novel, telling us the history of the werewolf pack, while focusing on the characters of Clay and Jeremy. Tales of the Otherworld is a little closer to what you’d expect from such a collection, delivering us the stories that couldn’t fit in the Otherworld novels. Like Men of the Otherworld, the short storie</span>
  <span id="freeText7666095386869004079" style="display:none">Tales of the Otherworld is the second collection of short fiction which takes place in the Otherworld universe. The first collection, Men of the Otherworld, was unique as it almost read like a novel, telling us the history of the werewolf pack, while focusing on the characters of Clay and Jeremy. Tales of the Otherworld is a little closer to what you’d expect from such a collection, delivering us the stories that couldn’t fit in the Otherworld novels. Like Men of the Otherworld, the short stories and novellas are arranged chronologically. Five are prequels to the Otherworld series, while remaining three take place during the actual series. The stories cover a wide amount of territory, giving us stories featuring major characters (such as Elena, Lucas and Clay) and characters that have so far played only supporting roles (such as Aaron, Logan, and Sean).<br /><br /><br />"Rebirth" is Aaron’s history story, telling us how he became a vampire and the first year of his vampire existence. This story is unique, as Armstrong doesn’t tend to focus on her vampire characters too much. Although there were places where I wish this story had been expanded upon a little it’s a well written short story that I enjoyed reading. <br /><br />Bewitched tells us the story about how black witch Eve Levine met and fell in love with the sorcerer Kristof Nast. This novella was particularly interesting as we got to see Eve when she was just starting off, and didn’t have the fearsome reputation that she ended up with in Haunted. Bewitched is a very character based story, and I really enjoyed watching the ways that Armstrong developed the relationship with Eve and Kris. This is the second novella featuring Eve to be published in the past year (the first being the stand alone, Angelic) and I find I like this one the best.<br /><br />"Birthright" features the character Logan, and shows how he discovered his werewolf heritage. "Birthright" is a relatively straightforward short story that it features a character that we don’t know too much about, although it lacks a bit in originality. Overall, it’s an enjoyable short piece.<br /><br />Beginnings is probably my favorite piece of the enter collection. The novella tells how us how Elena and Clay met while Elena was still in college. It follows their relationship as it grows from friendship to love, and the ends on the event that leads to where Elena ultimately ends up in Bitten. It was particularly interesting to read this after the most recent Otherworld novel, Frostbitten, which features the same characters roughly twenty years later, but in very different emotional states. Beginnings, like Men of the Otherworld, also shows how Clay has a hard time being human, and how the results can be interpreted as awkward or rude. It also results in the relationship between Elena and Clay being somewhat unhealthy. I loved how instead of writing this off as “true love,” the novella explores this unhealthy aspect of the relationships. This is especially interesting when compared to the character of Jason, Elena’s foster brother who is more outwardly starkerish and abusive.<br /><br />"Expectations" is a short story about a very young Lucas encountering Eve Levine. This story was interesting to read after Bewitched, as you get to see how Eve’s character had grown. Unfortunately, Lucas’s voice doesn’t really seem to be suited for the short story format, which occasionally marred my enjoyment of the story. <br /><br />"Ghosts" is a short story taken from Jeremy’s perspective, as he reflects on his decisions at the end of Beginnings. On one hand, it’s really interesting to see Jeremy’s views, but the story doesn’t have the ability to stand well on its own. I suspect someone picking the story up without having read Beginnings would be very confused. Those who have not read Bitten, may find themselves scratching their heads as well. <br /><br />"Wedding Bell Hell" is my favorite short story of the collection, and the only one that can be classified as humor. It tells the story of Paige and Lucas’s somewhat tumultuous roads to marriage. As someone who is planning on getting married in a year or two, I found this story to be equally amusing and terrifying, but was very happy that things ended well for my favorite couple of the series. <br /><br />The Case of El Chupacabra is the final novella in the collection, and tells the story of Paige and Lucas trying to track down a killer known as “El Chupacabra.” What I liked about this novella is the more character based moments, such as Lucas struggling with the fact that he feels that he’s not committing enough financially to family. I also enjoyed the exploration of the prejudice against vampires in the supernatural community. What I thought was somewhat lacking was the actual mystery itself, which wasn’t necessary bad, but not nearly as engrossing as the previous novellas in the collection. <br /><br />Although Tales of the Otherworld is not as consistent as Men of the Otherworld, it still delivers us a nice batch of short fiction. What I enjoy the most about the fiction displayed here is that Armstrong never seems to view the short story or novella format as a way to merely deliver cheap filler. Each story is filled with character development, or gives us a deeper view into the Otherworld universe. I hope that Armstrong will one day release a third volume in this series. I would love to see more short fiction and novellas in print.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7666095386869004079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_99157416" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99157416" />
    <a title="chucklesthescot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3426724-chucklesthescot"><img alt="chucklesthescot" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537360628p2/3426724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99157416?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chucklesthescot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chucklesthescot" href="/user/show/3426724-chucklesthescot">chucklesthescot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841499178" href="/book/show/7141610-tales-of-the-otherworld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=anthology">anthology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99157416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7900191391601779695">I waited until the series was finished before I read this anthology. It covers the meetings between popular couples-Aaron and Cassandra, Eve and Kristof and Clay and Elena. We also get the wedding of Paige and Lucas, Logan arriving at Stonehaven and Sean Nast gets himself into trouble at a murder scene. <br/><br/>Being a wolf fan, the main draw here for me was reading about Clay and Elena's story. It is great seeing another side of Clay and you can finally understand why he chose to bite Elena. I really e</span>
  <span id="freeText7900191391601779695" style="display:none">I waited until the series was finished before I read this anthology. It covers the meetings between popular couples-Aaron and Cassandra, Eve and Kristof and Clay and Elena. We also get the wedding of Paige and Lucas, Logan arriving at Stonehaven and Sean Nast gets himself into trouble at a murder scene. <br /><br />Being a wolf fan, the main draw here for me was reading about Clay and Elena's story. It is great seeing another side of Clay and you can finally understand why he chose to bite Elena. I really enjoyed the wedding story which was amusing! Seeing Logan in these stories makes me feel pretty sad as I like his character and I know what his later fate is. <br /><br />REBIRTH: (#0.01)<br />Aaron tries to stop a shopkeeper being robbed and is stabbed, waking up in a coffin where his mother explains about what a vampire is. If Aaron does not kill one human in his first year, he will die and as he gets near his time, he is considering picking death. Enter Cassandra.<br /><br />There is not enough Cassandra in the Otherworld so this short story was nice. Why couldn't they have sent her on a mission with Adam or the Pack during the series? She is much more fun than whiny Savannah!<br /><br />BEWITCHED: (#0.06)<br />Eve is being threatened by a client and Kristof offers to make the problem go away in exchange for magic lessons from her. This is the start of the forbidden relationship that leads to Savannah's problems with the Nast Cabal.<br /><br />This story was sad because Eve and Kris were such a great couple and for Kris to be cheated from seeing his daughter grow up by his evil family was heartbreaking. It also shows the good sides of Eve, trying to put Kris first so he did not lose his family and career over her.<br /><br />BIRTHRIGHT: (#0.07)<br />Logan has never known his father but a message is sent to him with Jeremy's address at Stonehaven. Clay, however believes that this is a mutt arriving to challenge Jeremy and is is ready to deal with him accordingly.<br /><br />Poor Logan goes to Stonehaven thinking this is the address of his dad and gets a few shocks from Clay on arrival! I liked this short story.<br /><br />BEGINNINGS: (#0.08)<br />Clay is regretting teaching a group of giggling students trying to seduce him-until Elena walks through the door. He offers her a job as his research assistant and they fall in love. But Elena has noticed that Clay is very possesive and when he beats up her stalker stepbrothers she is ready to dump him so Clay decides to take her to Stonehaven to tell her the truth-if Jeremy will allow it.<br /><br />We all know what happens next but it was nice to see how we got to The Bite. I had more sympathy for Clay after reading this-his anxiety at being parted from Elena overcoming his common sense. Seeing Jeremy so afraid and unable to stop Clay was quite gripping. The story also gives us more back story into Elena's abusive upbringing.<br /><br />EXPECTATIONS: (#0.11)<br />A man tells Lucas about a witch who has a dangerous book and Lucas agrees to go and get it. What he gets is a face to face fight with Eve.<br /><br />This was amusing, watching poor good guy Lucas getting his ass handed to him by Eve! Interesting story.<br /><br />GHOSTS: (#1.1)<br />Jeremy is plagued with doubts about the decisions he has been taking during the mutt uprising, and it forces him to look at the ghosts of his past.<br /><br />I liked this story as we see the Alpha unsure and vulnerable as he wonders what to do about the mutts. Of course, I love Jeremy so I'm always happy to see him in any story.<br /><br />WEDDING BELL HELL: (#4.1)<br />Paige and Lucas get anxious and stressed when the well meaning Benicio decides to 'help' with the wedding arrangements.<br /><br />This was a pretty amusing story. I like Benicio but he really knows how to make things worse! Poor Paige is already stressed enough without his interference!<br /><br />THE CASE OF EL CHUPACABRA: (#6.1)<br />Sean Nast is on business and visits a gay bar, stumbling across a murder victim, blamed on a local legend. He asks Paige, Lucas and Savannah to assist as the Cabals start fighting over a suspect in the crime.<br /><br />This was quite interesting, seeing Sean in the limelight for once. I liked all the twists and turns in the story though I could've done without Savannah stirring up trouble as usual.<br /><br />This was a good anthology and I liked the stories in it though I'd have liked Logan's story to be more of a novella size like the recent wolfie releases! Great anthology for fans of the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7900191391601779695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103228049" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103228049" />
    <a title="Tez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1090898-tez"><img alt="Tez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208410826p2/1090898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103228049?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tez" href="/user/show/1090898-tez">Tez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer103228049&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103228049" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4531526089616011816">Like <u>Men of the Otherworld</u>, <u>Tales of the Otherworld</u> is also an anthology of Kelley Armstrong's Otherworld-based short stories and novellas, which were previously free digitally on the author's website, but are now available from her regular publishers, with proceeds donated to World Literacy Canada. Since I'd read all but one of the stories before, they weren't fresh, and thus my enthusiasm for this tome is lower than perhaps it otherwise may have been.<br/><br/><u>Rebirth</u> is a great look at how Cassandra Du</span>
  <span id="freeText4531526089616011816" style="display:none">Like <u>Men of the Otherworld</u>, <u>Tales of the Otherworld</u> is also an anthology of Kelley Armstrong's Otherworld-based short stories and novellas, which were previously free digitally on the author's website, but are now available from her regular publishers, with proceeds donated to World Literacy Canada. Since I'd read all but one of the stories before, they weren't fresh, and thus my enthusiasm for this tome is lower than perhaps it otherwise may have been.<br /><br /><u>Rebirth</u> is a great look at how Cassandra DuCharme and Aaron Darnell met. <u>Bewitched</u> is an appealing romance between Eve Levine and Kristof Nast. <u>Birthright</u> still leaves a lot of questions about Logan Jonsen's paternal family. <u>Expectations</u> sees Lucas Cortez and Eve have a run-in. And <u>Ghosts</u> is more of a Jeremy Danvers vignette than a short story.<br /><br />But <u>Beginnings</u> is disturbing. Actually, more to the point, Clayton Danvers is disturbing: he treats Elena Michaels like a dog, he stalks her, and he turns her into a werewolf without her permission. As far as romances go, this is pretty effed-up. I'm not a big fan of romance fiction, because generally the characters don't work for me - as a couple, or individually. I really like Elena, but I've never liked Clay, so I don't respect Elena for hooking up with him. And staying together. And marrying, and having puppies human children. But perhaps the worst thing of all is that Elena knows this relationship isn't right. She's not stupid enough not to realise it, but she is stupid enough to continue the relationship.<br /><br /><i>First, Clay was possessive...Such behaviour was one of the four danger signs of an unhealthy relationship...Another sign was not wanting you to spend time with your friends...Or maybe I was rationalising away something I didn't want to see. Equally troubling was that Clay kept our relationship a secret from his family and friends...my gut was twisting, my brain feeding me all those little warnings I tried so hard not to hear, telling me something was wrong, wrong with us and wrong with him, and why the hell wasn't I taking the hint?</i><br /><br />And later:<br /><br /><i>How many times had I seen women in destructive relationships?...I'd seen women battered by abuse - physical, sexual, and psychological - and when asked why they stayed, so often their only defence was "I know he loves me." Until now, I'd never understood how you could cling to those words, that belief, and use it to wash away every misgiving. I had other talismans, too...He's never hit me. Never threatened to...except for last weekend, when he'd turned on me, hand raised, eyes blind with rage, knuckles brushing my cheek. But that had been a mistake. A mistake...So many excuses.</i><br /><br />Really, Elena should've hooked up with Logan or Nick.<br /><br />As for <u>The Case of El Chupacabra</u>...Lucas could really do with a sense of humour. I just don't like him. I like Sean Nast, and Cassandra, and I do like Savannah Levine in this story, but I suspect I may not like her point of view when she narrates the next two full-length Otherworld novels.<br /><br />Wait for the paperback of this collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4531526089616011816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_637539159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637539159" />
    <a title="Annie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310590-annie"><img alt="Annie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427209257p2/1310590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637539159?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/1310590-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637539159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15373848852260937370">This is a collection of Otherworld short stories and novellas. As a whole, I enjoyed it. If you've read the Otherworld series, you know that the books don't immediately follow right after each other. Time elapses and the characters lives continue (as they did prior to the start of Bitten), but we don't get to see it - they're dark places. You have to think of these stories as illuminating some of those dark places. They don't answer everything and they don't always have a neat, tidy ending, but </span>
  <span id="freeText15373848852260937370" style="display:none">This is a collection of Otherworld short stories and novellas. As a whole, I enjoyed it. If you've read the Otherworld series, you know that the books don't immediately follow right after each other. Time elapses and the characters lives continue (as they did prior to the start of Bitten), but we don't get to see it - they're dark places. You have to think of these stories as illuminating some of those dark places. They don't answer everything and they don't always have a neat, tidy ending, but we they give us more than we had before. And if you're a fan of Otherworld like me, you'll enjoy the illumination.<br /><br />Rebirth - Aaron's vampire origin story. I kinda get the feeling from this story that Aaron is a character Kelley liked and wished she could feature more in the main series. Since that didn't happen much, he gets his own short story.<br /><br />Bewitched - How Eve and Kristof met. I really enjoyed this particular story. Eve and Kristof were characters that I wasn't sure I liked (given Eve's dark magic and Kristof being a Cabal heir) until I read Haunted. Turned out that I really liked them as a couple. This short was icing on the cake in spite of the less-than-happy ending.<br /><br />Birthrights - How Logan got connected to the Pack. I liked everything about the story except the length. I wish it had been longer.<br /><br />Beginnings - How Clay and Elena met. I don't think I can say that I "like" this story because of the way it ends. This is the beginning of decade-long turmoil between Clay and Elena, which doesn't end until the end of Bitten. I love this couple and don't like to see them at odds. However, this story is important to understanding them as a couple, and it's encouraging to see how far both of them have come since that fateful time in Toronto.<br /><br />Expectations - In which Lucas attempts to steal a grimoire from Eve. There isn't much to this one, but it's almost guaranteed that I'll enjoy a story if Lucas is in it. <br /><br />Ghosts - During Bitten, Jeremy reflects on memories after sending Clay and Elena to Toronto. Too short, but I love getting more insight into Jeremy. After all this time, he's still such a mystery, and given that he only has two short stories from his POV, I think Kelley is keeping him one on purpose.<br /><br />Wedding Bell Hell - Paige and Lucas get married! This is a fun story that doesn't serve much purpose other than to delight the reader. Benicio is one of my favorite side characters and he doesn't disappoint. My only complaint is that I wish it had been longer.<br /><br />The Case of El Chupacabra - In which Sean hires Lucas and Paige to solve a murder. This story primarily deals with Sean's sexuality and how L&amp;P ended up with a former Cabal satellite office as their new headquarters. This one is long and the case itself wasn't my favorite. However, I do enjoy the interplay between Lucas and Benicio, especially as it pertains to the Cabal. It's also interesting to compare the Nasts with Benicio Cortez when it comes to the lifestyle choices their heirs want to make.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15373848852260937370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_179550901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179550901" />
    <a title="OpenBookSociety.com " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3540731-openbooksociety-com"><img alt="OpenBookSociety.com " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1270437893p2/3540731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179550901?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="OpenBookSociety.com " class="user" itemprop="url" name="OpenBookSociety.com " href="/user/show/3540731-openbooksociety-com">OpenBookSociety.com </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553907421" href="/book/show/7977671-tales-of-the-otherworld">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179550901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8948001961397446626">Review brought to you by OBS staff member Verushka<br/><br/>I first fell in love with Kelley Armstrong through Industrial Magic and Dime Store Magic, her novels featuring Paige Winterbourne. Paige was capable, strong, wielded magic and didn’t need leather to save the day. Don’t get me wrong, Armstrong is a fabulous writer and her Women of the Otherworld series is unique and engaging; but even as Paige led me to other books in the series, I found that I missed Paige, her voice and her life with Lucas and S</span>
  <span id="freeText8948001961397446626" style="display:none">Review brought to you by OBS staff member Verushka<br /><br />I first fell in love with Kelley Armstrong through Industrial Magic and Dime Store Magic, her novels featuring Paige Winterbourne. Paige was capable, strong, wielded magic and didn’t need leather to save the day. Don’t get me wrong, Armstrong is a fabulous writer and her Women of the Otherworld series is unique and engaging; but even as Paige led me to other books in the series, I found that I missed Paige, her voice and her life with Lucas and Savannah. Which means it’s been awhile since I’ve picked up a book with Armstrong’s name on the cover.<br /><br />And that is a pre-requisite if you are going to pick up Tales of the Otherworld, you have to be a fan of Armstrong’s other books, and to know her stories and characters well if you want to enjoy this book. That is a pity, because from my experience with her writing, these are wonderful looks into well-drawn out characters, filling in the bits and pieces her readers might have been curious about. Considering the theme of much of these stories is to give some sort of background to where her characters are in her full-length novels, slightly altered and geared towards getting new readers, this would have been a collection of memorable, new characters each one unique and well drawn out thanks to Armstrong’s talent and her love for the Otherworld she has created.<br /><br />There are stories of the “birth” of the supernatural aspects of some of her characters, i.e. being made into a vampire, or the literal birth of a werewolf character, for example. There is a mix of male and female characters from her series of novels, including Paige, whose I adored the most because I am terribly biased in my love for her. In that tale, we see Paige, Lucas and Savannah in the run up to their wedding, being beset upon by friends, relatives, in this case, Benicio and Maria Cortez, Lucas’ divorced parents. The story is laugh-out-loud funny, with an exasperated Lucas trying to control his father, and with Paige’s help finally succeeding in doing so with something very simple and very effective for Benicio. This story filled out Paige and Lucas’ story from the novels I’ve read so well, giving much also about Lucas and his own family life. Despite the supernatural nature of the characters, this was a tale of a very human wedding, which made it all the better.<br /><br />Kelley Armstrong has, in her Otherworld series, given readers a unique, wonderful and fabulously drawn out list of characters to enjoy and fall in love with. This is a great supplement to those novels, but in the end, knowledge of those books is a necessity to enjoy this gem.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://openbooksociety.com/article/kelley-armstrong-tales-of-the-otherworld-obs-book-review/">http://openbooksociety.com/article/ke...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8948001961397446626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130203271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130203271" />
    <a title="Adam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/718537-adam"><img alt="Adam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200528647p2/718537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130203271?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam" href="/user/show/718537-adam">Adam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/718537-adam?shelf=audiobooks-a-z">audiobooks-a-z</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130203271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8543175413316527570">Post listen review:<br/><br/>It seems that there are a lot of fans of this series. At least that is what it seems like from the amount of books the library has of these. I am not a fan. In this book there are a ton of werewolves, vampires, witches etc. So much so that they have councils and delegates to deal with supernatural inter-racial relations just to balance it all out. Everyone’s mother, sister, brother, cousin uncle, friend, fiancée etc. is one of these supernatural beings yet every time someone w</span>
  <span id="freeText8543175413316527570" style="display:none">Post listen review:<br /><br />It seems that there are a lot of fans of this series. At least that is what it seems like from the amount of books the library has of these. I am not a fan. In this book there are a ton of werewolves, vampires, witches etc. So much so that they have councils and delegates to deal with supernatural inter-racial relations just to balance it all out. Everyone’s mother, sister, brother, cousin uncle, friend, fiancée etc. is one of these supernatural beings yet every time someone who is not one finds out about any of it they are all shocked. And if they say find out that werewolves exist they are like ok that’s weird and makes me afraid but then don’t seem to think it possible that vampires exist. A lot of the characters also seem really whiney to me. But that is in the whole series not just this book. I listened to eleven discs of this. It is mostly short stories, some kind of long and some really short but most of them interrelate in some way. So I am going to summarize them all in one sentence to save the rest of you some time. I admit I tuned out here and there so I may have missed a character or two.<br /><br />I am a vampire/witch/werewolf/demon/sorcerer, whose life would be better if I could, not kill people/fall in love/find a life mate/get married/come out of the closet, but I can’t because my, relative/coven/pack/relative/cabal/family/friend/lover would think I am a killer/betrayer/animal/betrayer/betrayer and not manly, so instead I will only kill mercifully/run off and have the kid without him/bite her so she is a wolf too/find someone I can marry/come out of the closet, and everything goes wrong because I, am now accused of murder/am a single mother/realized that turning someone into a werewolf is not nice/still have to provide heirs and deny my sexuality due to sorcerers homophobia.<br />Other than that it was alright.<br /><br /><br />Pre-Listen guess: I hated Men of the Otherworld. I Bet I hate this one too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8543175413316527570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pG/R4ojT345o4mnFnSyNnkdRSC+fM+V4GgPnq6TB5erhaGTrl6dfNuo1jY4U7VmmGEVaMi3+67FhB3sfkybKUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9N/V3VuQkwjQbGpAej8/+xUXDUAjWvCoKMZN84rE1FCx2GDUROQTsFK7jgvz/uvDSgMfXZGX/mFTwtFHvSP76A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10651219850657862692">Kelley Armstrong has been telling stories since before she could write. Her earliest written efforts were disastrous. If asked for a story about girls and dolls, hers would invariably feature undead girls and evil dolls, much to her teachers' dismay. All efforts to make her produce "normal" stories failed.<br/><br/>Today, she continues to spin tales of ghosts and demons and werewolves, while safely locked a</span>
  <span id="freeText10651219850657862692" style="display:none">Kelley Armstrong has been telling stories since before she could write. Her earliest written efforts were disastrous. If asked for a story about girls and dolls, hers would invariably feature undead girls and evil dolls, much to her teachers' dismay. All efforts to make her produce "normal" stories failed.<br /><br />Today, she continues to spin tales of ghosts and demons and werewolves, while safely locked away in her basement writing dungeon. She's the author of the NYT-bestselling "Women of the Otherworld" paranormal suspense series and "Darkest Powers" young adult urban fantasy trilogy, as well as the Nadia Stafford crime series. Armstrong lives in southwestern Ontario with her husband, kids and far too many pets. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10651219850657862692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
